The following steps need to be taken during a natural calamity:',  - Be careful when handling animals, as they may be frightened or disorientated.',  - Make sure ', #', animals',  have clean water and food.',  - Evacuation is the best measure to prevent the animal from further suffering.',  - Provision of a shelter depends upon the type of natural calamity.',  - Feeding and watering of the animals should be adequate in order to meet the nutritional needs of the animals.',  - All injured animals should be treated promptly and antibiotics can be provided.',  - There is always a fear of disease spread in the herd which can be avoided through the mass vaccination programme.',  - Since many animals may die so disposal of dead animals can be a problem. In such cases do not through the animals rather the carcass should be buried or burned.',  - Contact your local vet regarding sick or injured animal.',  ', See more', +3', OLRDS',   ', 5 January at 16:30',   ', MINISTER FOR 100% RECRUITMENT OF LIs',  Agriculture and Farmers\u2019 Empowerment and Fisheries and Animal Resource Development Minister Pradeep Maharathy has asked the Animal Husbandry and Veterinary Services Director to ensure 100% recruitment of Livestock Inspectors.',  In a review meeting chaired by Maharathy and attended by Fisheries and Animal Resource Development Secretary Bishnupada Sethi recently, the Director said that so far 497 LIs have been recruited by the department.', ...',  Sethi advised the Director to submit a detailed proposal of further recruitment of LIs so that the Empowered Committee could be moved.',  The Director was also advised to ensure completion of livestock centres in a phased manner by the end of the February. Work in respect of 174 livestock centre is in progress.',  ', See more', See all', Videos', 86', 1', #FMD PREVENTIVE #VACCINATION.
 
Chief Minister Naveen Patnaik launched an ambitious programme on September 26 to cover all the livestock owned by farmers under preventive vaccination against the contagious foot and mouth disease (FMD). 

Cent percent vaccination for a period of five years will now be done in the State to cover entire bovine population. 
 
Similarly, #vaccination programme will be carried out against Anthrax, particularly in the 19 endemic districts to cover 19 lakh animals. 

The programme will include the provision of remuneration to farmers for reporting disease and for disposing the carcass of dead animal, massive awareness on safe handling and non-consumption of meat affected with Anthrax through mass media, preliminary and confirmatory diagnosis, surveillance, and research on Anthrax epidemiology in the State.  
 
By Dr. Gopal Tripathy', 58', 2', CONTROLLED BREEDING PROGRAMME IN #INDIGENOUS #CATTLE.

The Fisheries and Animal Resources Development Department has planned to initiate artificial insemination (AI) in 10,000 indigenous/ nondescript cows between October 2 and October 8.

This will be carried out by adopting advanced reproductive technology of synchronized breeding through camp mode with an objective to sensitize and motivate the farmers rearing Indigenous cattle. Chief Minister Naveen Patnaik launched the programme on September 26 at #Bhubaneswar.

By Dr. Gopal Tripathy', 87', 5', See all', Photos', See all', Posts', OLRDS',   ', 4 January at 16:30',   ', AVIAN INFLUENZA SURVEILLANCE ACTIVITIES',  The avian influenza surveillance activities by the government during 2016-17 has been quite satisfactory, as reports have revealed that most of the samples sent for testing to various laboratories over the months have tested negative for the disease.',  A total of 17,526 samples of swabs, ENV, serum and dead birds have been sent for testing to ADRI, Phulnakhara, RDDL (EL), Kolkata and NIHSAD, Bhopal before and after the outbreak of avian i', ...', nfluenza.',  Out of birds tested positive at NIHSAD and ADRI, just three were poultry birds.',  After bird flu was detected in Keranga village in Khordha district recently, the State Government has repeatedly assured to poultry farmers as well as consumers that there was no reason to panic and eating cooked chicken is quite safe. ',  The tests reiterate the government\u2019s stand.',  A total of 603 samples including nine dead birds, 285 swabs and 309 serum were sent to NIHSAD for testing on January 4 from Khordha, Sundargarh, Recognising the importance and purity of Odisha\u2019s native breed, the National Dairy Development Board (NDDB) has evinced interest to import five Jersey pure-bred breeding bulls from the state to improve the genetic potential of Indian cows under the National Dairy Plan (NDP).',  The NDDB had recently written a letter to the state government requesting to issue a no objection order.', ...',  Fisheries and Animal Resources Development Secretary ', #', Bishnupada',  Sethi has said that the state government has granted NDDB no objection order saying that the use of exotic Jersey semen will be in conformity with the breeding policy of Odisha.',  --',  ', See more', OLRDS',   ', 23 December 2016 at 16:30',   ', PARASAMANI ON  DISEASE OF GOAT ',  The latest episode of Parasamani telecast on 22-12-2016 at 7.30 pm is focussed on  Goat Pox, a disease of goats. The episode will be repeated on DD Odia at 9.30 PM on Saturday.',  Goat pox is a serious and often fatal viral disease of goats. It affects both young and adult goats. ', ...',  The symptoms are Fever, mucous discharge from eye and nose, respiratory distress and vesicles on lips, thigh, udder etc. ',  Goat pox can be prevented by administering goat pox vaccine @ 1 ml subcutaneously and repeated annually.',  The theme of this episode is to make the farmers aware about goat pox disease, its symptoms, seriousness, economic loss and the measures that should be taken to prevent the occurrence of the disease.',  ', See more', See more', People', 143,016 ', likes', 5',  ', visits', About', Odisha Livestock Resources Development Society(OLRDS) OBPI Campus, The following steps need to be taken during a natural calamity:',  - Be careful when handling animals, as they may be frightened or disorientated.',  - Make sure ', #', animals',  have clean water and food.',  - Evacuation is the best measure to prevent the animal from further suffering.',  - Provision of a shelter depends upon the type of natural calamity.',  - Feeding and watering of the animals should be adequate in order to meet the nutritional needs of the animals.',  - All injured animals should be treated promptly and antibiotics can be provided.',  - There is always a fear of disease spread in the herd which can be avoided through the mass vaccination programme.',  - Since many animals may die so disposal of dead animals can be a problem. Work in respect of 174 livestock centre is in progress.',  ', See more', See all', Videos', 86', 1', #FMD PREVENTIVE #VACCINATION.
 
Chief Minister Naveen Patnaik launched an ambitious programme on September 26 to cover all the livestock owned by farmers under preventive vaccination against the contagious foot and mouth disease (FMD). 

Cent percent vaccination for a period of five years will now be done in the State to cover entire bovine population. 
 
Similarly, #vaccination programme will be carried out against Anthrax, particularly in the 19 endemic districts to cover 19 lakh animals. 

The programme will include the provision of remuneration to farmers for reporting disease and for disposing the carcass of dead animal, massive awareness on safe handling and non-consumption of meat affected with Anthrax through mass media, preliminary and confirmatory diagnosis, surveillance, and research on Anthrax epidemiology in the State.  
 
By Dr. Gopal Tripathy', 58', 2', CONTROLLED BREEDING PROGRAMME IN #INDIGENOUS #CATTLE.

The Fisheries and Animal Resources Development Department has planned to initiate artificial insemination (AI) in 10,000 indigenous/ nondescript cows between October 2 and October 8.

This will be carried out by adopting advanced reproductive technology of synchronized breeding through camp mode with an objective to sensitize and motivate the farmers rearing Indigenous cattle. Chief Minister Naveen Patnaik launched the programme on September 26 at #Bhubaneswar.

Recognising the importance and purity of Odisha\u2019s native breed, the National Dairy Development Board (NDDB) has evinced interest to import five Jersey pure-bred breeding bulls from the state to on 22-12-2016 at 7.30 pm is focussed on  Goat Pox, a disease of goats. The episode will be repeated on DD Odia at 9.30 PM on Saturday.',  Goat pox is a serious and often fatal viral disease of goats. It affects both young and adult goats. ', ...',  The symptoms are Fever, mucous discharge from eye and nose, respiratory distress and vesicles on lips, thigh, udder etc. ',  Goat pox can be prevented by administering goat pox vaccine @ 1 ml subcutaneously and repeated annually.',  The theme of this episode is to make the farmers aware about goat pox disease, its symptoms, seriousness, economic loss and the measures that should be
